Something like\n pkgconf --define-variable=prefix=/home/user/installpath --variable=systemdsystemunitdir systemd\n\nI\m not convinced that this entirely useful because the installed systemd will\nnot look at those paths but maybe it\s OK as an alternative type of $DESTDIR.\nThis has been requested a few times over the years so let\s just provide this.\n\nI thought this would be more complicated since we allow all kinds of directories\nto be overrides in the compilation configuration. But it turns out that all the\ndirectories defined in systemd.pc are relative to three prefixes:\n$prefix $rootprefix and $sysconfdir. So this patch adds $rootprefix and $sysconfdir\nto the .pc file and then changes the subsequent definitions in the .pc file to use\nthem. In the end we define each path twice using the same rules: once in meson.build\nand once in the .pc file.\n\nWithout overrides:\n$ for i in $pkgconf --with-path=build/src/core systemd --print-variables; do\n echo -n "$i = "; pkgconf --with-path=$PWD/build/src/core --variable=$i systemd\n done\ncontaineruidbasemax = 1878982656\ncontaineruidbasemin = 524288\ndynamicuidmax = 65519\ndynamicuidmin = 61184\nsystemgidmax = 999\nsystemuidmax = 999\ncatalogdir = /usr/lib/systemd/catalog\nmodulesloaddir = /usr/lib/modules-load.d\nbinfmtdir = /usr/lib/binfmt.d\nsysctldir = /usr/lib/sysctl.d\nsysusersdir = /usr/lib/sysusers.d\ntmpfilesdir = /usr/lib/tmpfiles.d\nsystemdshutdowndir = /usr/lib/systemd/system-shutdown\nsystemdsleepdir = /usr/lib/systemd/system-sleep\nsystemdusergeneratordir = /usr/lib/systemd/user-generators\nsystemdsystemgeneratordir = /usr/lib/systemd/system-generators\nsystemduserunitpath = /etc/systemd/user:/etc/systemd/user:/run/systemd/user:/usr/local/lib/systemd/user:/usr/local/share/systemd/user:/usr/lib/systemd/user:/usr/lib/systemd/user:/usr/share/systemd/user\nsystemdsystemunitpath = /etc/systemd/system:/etc/systemd/system:/run/systemd/system:/usr/local/lib/systemd/system:/usr/lib/systemd/system:/usr/lib/systemd/system:/lib/systemd/system\nsystemduserconfdir = /etc/systemd/user\nsystemdsystemconfdir = /etc/systemd/system\nsystemduserpresetdir = /usr/lib/systemd/user-preset\nsystemduserunitdir = /usr/lib/systemd/user\nsystemdsystempresetdir = /usr/lib/systemd/system-preset\nsystemdsystemunitdir = /usr/lib/systemd/system\nsystemdutildir = /usr/lib/systemd\nsysconfdir = /etc\nrootprefix = /usr\nprefix = /usr\npcfiledir = /usr/share/pkgconfig\n\nWith overrides:\n$ for i in $pkgconf --with-path=build/src/core systemd --print-variables; do\n echo -n "$i = "; pkgconf --with-path=$PWD/build/src/core \\\n --define-variable=prefix=/PREFIX \\\n --define-variable=rootprefix=/ROOTPREFIX \\\n --define-variable=sysconfdir=/SYSCONF --variable=$i systemd\n done\ncontaineruidbasemax = 1878982656\ncontaineruidbasemin = 524288\ndynamicuidmax = 65519\ndynamicuidmin = 61184\nsystemgidmax = 999\nsystemuidmax = 999\ncatalogdir = /PREFIX/lib/systemd/catalog\nmodulesloaddir = /PREFIX/lib/modules-load.d\nbinfmtdir = /PREFIX/lib/binfmt.d\nsysctldir = /PREFIX/lib/sysctl.d\nsysusersdir = /PREFIX/lib/sysusers.d\ntmpfilesdir = /PREFIX/lib/tmpfiles.d\nsystemdshutdowndir = /ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system-shutdown\nsystemdsleepdir = /ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system-sleep\nsystemdusergeneratordir = /PREFIX/lib/systemd/user-generators\nsystemdsystemgeneratordir = /ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system-generators\nsystemduserunitpath = /SYSCONF/systemd/user:/etc/systemd/user:/run/systemd/user:/usr/local/lib/systemd/user:/usr/local/share/systemd/user:/PREFIX/lib/systemd/user:/usr/lib/systemd/user:/usr/share/systemd/user\nsystemdsystemunitpath = /SYSCONF/systemd/system:/etc/systemd/system:/run/systemd/system:/usr/local/lib/systemd/system:/ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system:/usr/lib/systemd/system:/lib/systemd/system\nsystemduserconfdir = /SYSCONF/systemd/user\nsystemdsystemconfdir = /SYSCONF/systemd/system\nsystemduserpresetdir = /PREFIX/lib/systemd/user-preset\nsystemduserunitdir = /PREFIX/lib/systemd/user\nsystemdsystempresetdir = /ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system-preset\nsystemdsystemunitdir = /ROOTPREFIX/lib/systemd/system\nsystemdutildir = /usr/lib/systemd\nsysconfdir = /SYSCONF\nrootprefix = /ROOTPREFIX\nprefix = /PREFIX\npcfiledir = /usr/share/pkgconfig\n\npkgconf doesn\t provide a way to print all variables together with their definitions\naccording to the man page. While\nthis is normally enough for the case of the backend this can confuse\ncallers of this routine on Windows as all errors would map to the same\nbehavior. So for example even permission errors would be thought as\nhaving an empty directory while there could be contents in it.\n\nThis commit changes the error handling so as readdir gets a behavior\nsimilar to native implementations: force errno=0 when seeing\nERROR_FILE_NOT_FOUND as error and consider other errors as plain\nfailures.\n\nWhile looking at the patch I noticed that MinGW does not enforce\nerrno=0 when looking at the first file but it gets enforced on the next\nfile lookups. This means that multiple standbys cannot be\ndistinguished easily on a primary for example in pg_stat_activity or\nsynchronous_standby_names.\n\nIf cluster_name is set use that for fallback_application_name in the\nwalreceiver. If it\s not set it remains "walreceiver". If someone\nset cluster_name to identify their instance we might as well use that\nby default to identify the node remotely as well. It\s still possible\nto specify another application_name in primary_conninfo explicitly.\n\nReviewed-by: Euler Taveira <euler@timbira.com.br>\nDiscussion: https://www.postgresql.org/message-id/flat/1257eaee-4874-e791-e83a-46720c72cac7@2ndquadrant.com"},
{"repo_url":"https://github.com/postgresql-cfbot/postgresql.git","repo_name":"postgresql","fixed_hash":"87c346a35ee869e401e736163ec9d21632cc3b0d","buggy_hash":"da35d14806249c4619b2b5efda061211768a27ce","commit_msg":"Fix SCRAM authentication via SSL when mixing versions of OpenSSL\n\nWhen using a libpq client linked with OpenSSL 1.0.1 or older to connect\nto a backend linked with OpenSSL 1.0.2 or newer the server would send\nSCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS and SCRAM-SHA-256 as valid mechanisms for the SASL\nexchange and the client would choose SCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS even if it does\nnot support channel binding leading to a confusing error. In this\ncase what the client ought to do is switch to SCRAM-SHA-256 so as the\nauthentication can move on and succeed.\n\nSo for a SCRAM authentication over SSL here are all the cases present\nand how we deal with them using libpq:\n1 Server supports channel binding it sends SCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS and\nSCRAM-SHA-256 as allowed mechanisms.\n1-1 Client supports channel binding chooses SCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS.\n1-2 Client does not support channel binding chooses SCRAM-SHA-256.\n2 Server does not support channel binding sends SCRAM-SHA-256 as\nallowed mechanism.\n2-1 Client supports channel binding still it has no choice but to\nchoose SCRAM-SHA-256.\n2-2 Client does not support channel binding it chooses SCRAM-SHA-256.\nIn all these scenarios the connection should succeed and the one which\nwas handled incorrectly prior this commit is 1-2 causing the\nconnection attempt to fail because client chose SCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS over\nSCRAM-SHA-256.\n\nReported-by: Hugh Ranalli\nDiagnosed-by: Peter Eisentraut\nAuthor: Michael Paquier\nReviewed-by: Peter Eisentraut\nDiscussion: https://postgr.es/m/CAAhbUMO89SqUk-5mMY+OapgWf-twF2NA5sCucbHEzMfGbvcepA@mail.gmail.com\nBackpatch-through: 11"},

Also invent forfour and\nforfive macros to do the same for four or five parallel lists\nand use those where applicable.\n\nThe immediate motivation for doing this is to reduce the number\nof ad-hoc lnext calls to reduce the footprint of a WIP patch.\nHowever it seems like good cleanup and error-proofing anyway;\nthe places that were combining forthree with a manually iterated\nloop seem particularly illegible and bug-prone.\n\nThere was some speculation about restructuring related parsetree\nrepresentations to reduce the need for parallel list chasing of\nthis sort. {"repo_url":"https://github.com/horms2/ovs.git","repo_name":"ovs","fixed_hash":"e4a87e07ad5c8d1ea69bef13031c00b2c40d11df","buggy_hash":"ac18af5bf4648d06abfd7095ac5a5c4e914ab6f4","commit_msg":""OVN: Use offset instead of pointer into ofpbuf\n\nIn general maintaining a pointer into an ofpbuf is risky. As the ofpbuf\ngrows it can reallocate its data. If this happens then pointers into\nthe data will become invalid.\n\nA safer practice is to track an offset into the ofpbufs data where a\nstructure you are interested in is kept. This way if the ofpbuf data is\nreallocated you can find your structure again by using the offset.\n\nIn practice this patch is not fixing any issues with OVN. Even though\nthe ra pointer is pointing to ofpbuf data that can be reallocated it\nwill never actually happen. ovn-northd and all test cases always encode\nthe address mode first meaning we will only ever read from the ra\npointer before the ofpbuf has a chance to expand.\n\nHowever this base work is essential for an upcoming patch in this series.\n\nSigned-off-by: Mark Michelson <mmichels@redhat.com>\nSigned-off-by: Ben Pfaff <blp@ovn.org>""},
{"repo_url":"https://github.com/horms2/ovs.git","repo_name":"ovs","fixed_hash":"6a979c76eef08339122346455dbf1519a32e7c0b","buggy_hash":"e4a87e07ad5c8d1ea69bef13031c00b2c40d11df","commit_msg":"OVN: Always send prefix option in RAs\n\nOVN\s behavior when sending router advertisements has been to include IP\nprefix information only if the address mode is set to "slaac" or\n"dhcp_stateless". In these modes sending the prefix to the client is\nnecessary so that it may automatically provision its IP address. We do\nnot send the prefix option when the address mode is set to\n"dhcp_stateful" since there is no need for the client to automatically\nprovision an IP address.\n\nThis logic is flawed however. When using dhcp_stateful we provide a\nmanaged IPv6 address for a client. However because we do not provide\nprefix information in our RAs the client does not know the prefix\nlength for the address it has been allocated. With dhclient we have\nseen it assume either /64 or /128 depending on which version is being\nused. This may not accurately reflect the prefix length being used by\nthe DHCP server though.\n\nThe fix here is to always send prefix information in our RAs regardless\nof address mode. The key difference lies in how we set the A\nautonomous addressing flag. For slaac and dhcp_stateless address\nmodes we will set this flag indicating the client should provision its\nown address based on the prefix we have sent. For dhcp_stateful we will\nnot set this flag. This way it is clear the prefix is informational\nand the client should not try to provision its own IPv6 address.\n\nSigned-off-by: Mark Michelson <mmichels@redhat.com>\nSigned-off-by: Ben Pfaff <blp@ovn.org>"},
{"repo_url":"https://github.com/horms2/ovs.git","repo_name":"ovs","fixed_hash":"861f2824cac72aee628d5ff623c3a5c531bd3422","buggy_hash":"6a979c76eef08339122346455dbf1519a32e7c0b","commit_msg":"OVN: Make periodic RAs consistent with RA responder.\n\nThis commit makes periodic RAs from OVN consistent with the RAs sent in\nresponse to RSs. Specifically this ensures that prefix flags are set\ncorrectly for each address mode.\n\nThis commit also gets rid of some redundant definitions for RA prefix\noption flags from packets.h in favor of the ones in ovn-l7.h.\n\nSigned-off-by: Mark Michelson <mmichels@redhat.com>\nSigned-off-by: Ben Pfaff <blp@ovn.org>"},

{"repo_url":"https://github.com/nathawes/swift.git","repo_name":"swift","fixed_hash":"6ab83122acf6cc8f98e24a3d47e62483d63c4df9","buggy_hash":"9b0a94fb62d0864a63d84c63f93189411de59740","commit_msg":""Fix storeEnumTagSinglePayload on big-endian systems\n\nThe part of the tag stored in the payload can currently be up to\n8 bytes in size though only the low 4 bytes can be non-zero.\nOn little-endian machines this doesnt matter we can always just\nstore up to 4 bytes and zero the remaining payload bytes. On big-\nendian systems however we may need to store more than 4 bytes.\n\nThe store implementation now mirrors the runtime code that fetches\nthe tag on big-endian systems which already treats the payload tag\nas an 8 byte integer.\n\nThis is a spot fix but longer term we might want to consider\nrefactoring this code to reduce the number of differences between\nbig- and little-endian implementations. For example we could\ncentralise some of the copying logic and/or make the payload tag\na 4 byte field on all platforms.""},

Note that the ClassLoader class is registered as parallel capable by default. However its subclasses still need to register themselves if they are parallel capable. ``\n i.e we can have finer class loading locks by registering classloaders as parallel capable. {"repo_url":"https://github.com/postgres/postgres.git","repo_name":"postgres","fixed_hash":"d70c147fa217c4bae32ac1afb86ab42d98b36fdf","buggy_hash":"7988cb446d20512ec9d091db66dba6adee3f3d4b","commit_msg":""Avoid crash in partitionwise join planning under GEQO.\n\nWhile trying to plan a partitionwise join we may be faced with cases\nwhere one or both input partitions for a particular segment of the join\nhave been pruned away. In HEAD and v11 this is problematic because\nearlier processing didnt bother to make a pruned RelOptInfo fully\nvalid. With an upcoming patch to make partition pruning more efficient\nthisll be even more problematic because said RelOptInfo wont exist at\nall.\n\nThe existing code attempts to deal with this by retroactively making the\nRelOptInfo fully valid but that causes crashes under GEQO because join\nplanning is done in a short-lived memory context. In v11 we could\nprobably have fixed this by switching to the planners main context\nwhile fixing up the RelOptInfo but that idea doesnt scale well to the\nupcoming patch. It would be better not to mess with the base-relation\ndata structures during join planning anyway --- thats just a recipe\nfor order-of-operations bugs.\n\nIn many cases though we dont actually need the child RelOptInfo\nbecause if the input is certainly empty then the join segments result\nis certainly empty so we can skip making a join plan altogether. The\nexisting code ultimately arrives at the same conclusion but only after\ndoing a lot more work. This approach works except when the pruned-away\npartition is on the nullable side of a LEFT ANTI or FULL join and the\nother side isnt pruned. But in those cases the existing code leaves a\nlot to be desired anyway --- the correct output is just the result of\nthe unpruned side of the join but we were emitting a useless outer join\nagainst a dummy Result. Pending somebody writing code to handle that\nmore nicely lets just abandon the partitionwise-join optimization in\nsuch cases.\n\nWhen the modified code skips making a join plan it doesnt make a\njoin RelOptInfo either; this requires some upper-level code to\ncope with nulls in part_rels arrays. We would have had to have\nthat anyway after the upcoming patch.\n\nBack-patch to v11 since the crash is demonstrable there.\n\nDiscussion: https://postgr.es/m/8305.1553884377@sss.pgh.pa.us""},
